	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">FA Cup</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="FA Cup (disambiguation)">FA Cup (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<table class="infobox football" style="width:22em"><caption>FA Cup</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Fa_cup.svg" class="image"><img alt="Fa cup.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/33px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png" decoding="async" width="33" height="33" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/50px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/66px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="60" data-file-height="60" /> <i><a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_FA_Cup" title="2019–20 FA Cup">2019–20 FA Cup</a></i></td></tr></tbody></table> 
<p><b>The FA Cup</b>, also known officially as <b>The Football Association Challenge Cup</b>, is an annual <a href="/wiki/Single-elimination_tournament" title="Single-elimination tournament">knockout</a> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> competition in men's domestic <a href="/wiki/Football_in_England" title="Football in England">English football</a>. First played during the <a href="/wiki/1871%E2%80%9372_FA_Cup" title="1871–72 FA Cup">1871–72 season</a>, it is the <a href="/wiki/Oldest_football_competitions" title="Oldest football competitions">oldest national football competition</a>  in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> It is organised by and named after <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a> (The FA). Since 2015, it has been known as <b>The Emirates FA Cup</b> after its headline sponsor. A concurrent <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_association_football" title="Women&#39;s association football">women's</a> tournament is also held, the <a href="/wiki/FA_Women%27s_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Women&#39;s Cup">FA Women's Cup</a>.
</p><p>The competition is open to any eligible <a href="/wiki/Football_club" class="mw-redirect" title="Football club">club</a> down to Level 10 of the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a> – all 92 professional clubs in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> (Level 1) and the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">English Football League</a> (Levels 2 to 4), and several hundred "non-league" teams in Steps 1 to 6 of the <a href="/wiki/National_League_System" title="National League System">National League System</a> (Levels 5 to 10).<sup id="cite_ref-:12_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> A record 763 clubs competed in <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_FA_Cup" title="2011–12 FA Cup">2011–12</a>. The tournament consists of 12 randomly drawn rounds followed by <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_semi-finals" title="FA Cup semi-finals">the semi-finals</a> and <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">the final</a>. Entrants are not <a href="/wiki/Seed_(sports)" title="Seed (sports)">seeded</a>, although a system of <a href="/wiki/Bye_(sports)" title="Bye (sports)">byes</a> based on league level ensures higher ranked teams enter in later rounds – the minimum number of games needed to win, depending on which round a team enters the competition, ranges from six to fourteen.
</p><p>The first six rounds are the Qualifying Competition, from which 32 teams progress to the first round of the Competition Proper, meeting the first of the 48 professional teams from <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_One" title="EFL League One">Leagues One</a> and <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_Two" title="EFL League Two">Two</a>. The last entrants are the Premier League and <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> clubs, into the draw for the Third Round Proper.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In the modern era, only one non-league team has ever reached the quarter-finals, and teams below Level 2 have never reached the final.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;note 1&#93;</a></sup> As a result, significant focus is given to the smaller teams who progress furthest, especially if they achieve an unlikely "giant-killing" victory.
</p><p>Winners receive the FA Cup trophy, of which there have been two designs and five actual cups; the latest is a 2014 replica of the second design, introduced in 1911. Winners also qualify for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">the Europa League</a> and a place in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">FA Community Shield</a> match. <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> are the current holders, having beaten <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> 6–0 in the <a href="/wiki/2019_FA_Cup_Final" title="2019 FA Cup Final">2019 final</a>. <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F._C." class="mw-redirect" title="Arsenal F. C.">Arsenal</a> are the most successful club with 13 titles. <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> is the most successful manager in the history of the competition, having won seven finals as manager of <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal F.C.</a>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_FA_Cup" title="History of the FA Cup">History of the FA Cup</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FACupFinal1905NewcastleVilla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/FACupFinal1905NewcastleVilla.jpg/250px-FACupFinal1905NewcastleVilla.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/FACupFinal1905NewcastleVilla.jpg/375px-FACupFinal1905NewcastleVilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/FACupFinal1905NewcastleVilla.jpg/500px-FACupFinal1905NewcastleVilla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="728" data-file-height="477" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FACupFinal1905NewcastleVilla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Harry_Hampton_(footballer,_born_1885)" title="Harry Hampton (footballer, born 1885)">Harry Hampton</a> scores one of his two goals in the <a href="/wiki/1905_FA_Cup_Final" title="1905 FA Cup Final">1905 FA Cup Final</a> where <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1863, the newly founded <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">Football Association</a> (the FA) published the <a href="/wiki/Laws_of_the_Game_(association_football)" title="Laws of the Game (association football)">Laws of the Game</a> of Association Football, unifying the various different rules in use before then. On 20 July 1871, in the offices of <a href="/wiki/The_Sportsman_(1865_newspaper)" title="The Sportsman (1865 newspaper)"><i>The Sportsman</i> newspaper</a>, the FA Secretary <a href="/wiki/C._W._Alcock" class="mw-redirect" title="C. W. Alcock">C. W. Alcock</a> proposed to the FA committee that "it is desirable that a Challenge Cup should be established in connection with the Association for which all clubs belonging to the Association should be invited to compete". The <a href="/wiki/1871%E2%80%9372_FA_Cup" title="1871–72 FA Cup">inaugural FA Cup tournament</a> kicked off in November 1871. After thirteen games in all, <a href="/wiki/Wanderers_F.C." title="Wanderers F.C.">Wanderers</a> were crowned the winners in the final, on 16 March 1872. Wanderers retained the trophy the following year. The modern cup was beginning to be established by the 1888–89 season, when qualifying rounds were introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/1914%E2%80%9315_FA_Cup" title="1914–15 FA Cup">1914–15</a> edition, the competition was suspended due to the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First World War</a>, and did not resume until <a href="/wiki/1919%E2%80%9320_FA_Cup" title="1919–20 FA Cup">1919–20</a>. The <a href="/wiki/1923_FA_Cup_Final" title="1923 FA Cup Final">1923 FA Cup Final</a>, commonly known as the "White Horse Final", was the first final to be played in the newly opened <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> (known at the time as the Empire Stadium). The <a href="/wiki/1927_FA_Cup_Final" title="1927 FA Cup Final">1927 final</a> saw "<a href="/wiki/Abide_with_Me" title="Abide with Me">Abide with Me</a>" being sung for the first time at the Cup final, which has become a pre-match tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Due to the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the competition was not played between the <a href="/wiki/1938%E2%80%9339_FA_Cup" title="1938–39 FA Cup">1938–39</a> and <a href="/wiki/1945%E2%80%9346_FA_Cup" title="1945–46 FA Cup">1945–46</a> editions. Due to the wartime breaks, the competition did not celebrate its centenary year until <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_FA_Cup" title="1980–81 FA Cup">1980–81</a>; fittingly the final featured a goal by <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Villa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ricky Villa">Ricky Villa</a> which was later voted the greatest goal ever scored at Wembley Stadium, but has since been replaced by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gerrard" title="Steven Gerrard">Steven Gerrard</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having previously featured replays, the modern day practice of ensuring the semi-final and final matches finish on the day was introduced in 2000. Redevelopment of Wembley saw the final played outside of England for the first time, the 2001–2006 finals being played at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>. The final returned to Wembley in 2007, followed by the semi-finals from 2008.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Eligibility">Eligibility</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Eligibility">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The competition is open to any club down to Level 10 of the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a> which meets the eligibility criteria. All clubs in the top four levels (the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> and the three divisions of the <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">Football League</a>) are automatically eligible. Clubs in the next six levels (<a href="/wiki/Non-league_football" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-league football">non-league football</a>) are also eligible provided they have played in either the FA Cup, <a href="/wiki/FA_Trophy" title="FA Trophy">FA Trophy</a> or <a href="/wiki/FA_Vase" title="FA Vase">FA Vase</a> competitions in the previous season. Newly formed clubs, such as <a href="/wiki/F.C._United_of_Manchester" title="F.C. United of Manchester">F.C. United of Manchester</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_FA_Cup" title="2005–06 FA Cup">2005–06</a> and also <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_FA_Cup" title="2006–07 FA Cup">2006–07</a>, may not therefore play in the FA Cup in their first season. All clubs entering the competition must also have a suitable stadium.
</p><p>It is very rare for top clubs to miss the competition, although it can happen in exceptional circumstances. <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> did not defend their title in <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_FA_Cup" title="1999–2000 FA Cup">1999–2000</a>, as they were already in the <a href="/wiki/2000_FIFA_Club_World_Championship" title="2000 FIFA Club World Championship">inaugural</a> <a href="/wiki/FIFA_Club_World_Cup" title="FIFA Club World Cup">Club World Championship</a>. The club stated that entering both tournaments would overload their fixture schedule and make it more difficult to defend their Champions League and Premier League titles. The club claimed that they did not want to devalue the FA Cup by fielding a weaker side. The move benefited United as they received a two-week break and won the 1999–2000 league title by an 18-point margin, although they did not progress past the group stage of the Club World Championship. The withdrawal from the FA Cup, however, drew considerable criticism as this weakened the tournament's prestige and <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Sir Alex Ferguson</a> later admitted his regret regarding their handling of the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Welsh sides that play in English leagues are eligible, although since the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Welsh Premier League">League of Wales</a> there are only five clubs remaining: <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> (the only non-English team to win the tournament, in <a href="/wiki/1927_FA_Cup_Final" title="1927 FA Cup Final">1927</a>), <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newport_County_A.F.C." title="Newport County A.F.C.">Newport County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Wrexham F.C.">Wrexham</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Merthyr_Town_F.C." title="Merthyr Town F.C.">Merthyr Town</a>. In the early years other teams from Wales, Ireland and Scotland also took part in the competition, with Glasgow side <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_F.C." title="Queen&#39;s Park F.C.">Queen's Park</a> losing the final to <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers" class="mw-redirect" title="Blackburn Rovers">Blackburn Rovers</a> in <a href="/wiki/1884_FA_Cup_Final" title="1884 FA Cup Final">1884</a> and <a href="/wiki/1885_FA_Cup_Final" title="1885 FA Cup Final">1885</a> before being barred from entering by the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Association" title="Scottish Football Association">Scottish Football Association</a>. In the 2013–14 season the first <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Island</a> club entered the competition when <a href="/wiki/Guernsey_F.C." title="Guernsey F.C.">Guernsey F.C.</a> competed.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The number of entrants has increased greatly in recent years. In the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_2004%E2%80%9305" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Cup 2004–05">2004–05</a> season, 660 clubs entered the competition, beating the long-standing record of 656 from the 1921–22 season. In <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_FA_Cup" title="2005–06 FA Cup">2005–06</a> this increased to 674 entrants, in <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_FA_Cup" title="2006–07 FA Cup">2006–07</a> to 687, in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_FA_Cup" title="2007–08 FA Cup">2007–08</a> to 731 clubs, and for the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_FA_Cup" title="2008–09 FA Cup">2008–09</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_FA_Cup" title="2009–10 FA Cup">2009–10</a> competitions it reached 762.<sup id="cite_ref-record_number_of_entries_for_2008/9_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-record_number_of_entries_for_2008/9-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The number has varied slightly but remained roughly stable since then, with 759 clubs participating in <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_FA_Cup" title="2010–11 FA Cup">2010–11</a>, a record 763 in <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_FA_Cup" title="2011–12 FA Cup">2011–12</a>, 758 for <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_FA_Cup" title="2012–13 FA Cup">2012–13</a>, 737 for <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_FA_Cup" title="2013–14 FA Cup">2013–14</a> and 736 for <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_FA_Cup" title="2014–15 FA Cup">2014–15</a>. By comparison, the other major English domestic cup, the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a>, involves only the 92 members of the Premier League and Football League.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_format">Competition format</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Competition format">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beginning in August, the competition proceeds as a <a href="/wiki/Knockout_tournament" class="mw-redirect" title="Knockout tournament">knockout tournament</a> throughout, consisting of twelve rounds, a semi-final and then a final, in May. A system of byes ensures clubs above Level 9 and 10 enter the competition at later stages. There is no <a href="/wiki/Seed_(tennis)" class="mw-redirect" title="Seed (tennis)">seeding</a>, the fixtures in each round being determined by a random draw. Prior to the fifth round, fixtures ending in a tie are replayed once only.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The first six rounds are qualifiers, with the draws organised on a regional basis. The next six rounds are the "proper" rounds where all clubs are in one draw.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schedule">Schedule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Schedule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Entrants from the bottom two levels (9 and 10) begin the competition in the Extra Preliminary Round. Clubs from higher levels are then added in later rounds, as per the table below. The months in which rounds are played are traditional, with exact dates subject to each year's calendar.
</p>

<p>The qualifying rounds are regionalised to reduce the travel costs for smaller non-league sides. The first and second proper rounds were also previously split into Northern and Southern sections, but this practice was ended after the 1997–98 competition.
</p><p>The final is normally held the Saturday after the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> season finishes in May. The only seasons in recent times when this pattern was not followed were <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_in_English_football" title="1999–2000 in English football">1999–2000</a>, when most rounds were played a few weeks earlier than normal as an experiment, and <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_in_English_football" title="2010–11 in English football">2010–11</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_in_English_football" title="2012–13 in English football">2012–13</a> when the FA Cup Final was played before the Premier League season had finished, to allow <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> to be ready for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> final,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> as well as in <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_in_English_football" title="2011–12 in English football">2011–12</a> to allow England time to prepare for that summer's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">European Championships</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_draw">The draw</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The draw">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The draws for the Extra-Preliminary, Preliminary, and First Qualifying Rounds used to all occur at the same time. Thereafter, the draw for each subsequent round is not made until after the scheduled dates for the previous round, meaning that in the case of replays, clubs will often know their future opponents in advance. This season 2016/17 the draw for the 1st qualifying round was drawn at a later date as per previous season's later rounds.
</p><p>The draw for each of the proper rounds is broadcast live on television, usually taking place at the conclusion of live coverage of one of the games of the previous round. Public interest is particularly high during the draw for the third round, which is where the top-ranked teams are added to the draw.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tiebreaking">Tiebreaking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tiebreaking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In rounds up to and including the Fourth Round Proper, fixtures resulting in a draw (after normal time) go to a <a href="/wiki/Replay_(sports)" title="Replay (sports)">replay</a>, played at the venue of the away team, at a later date; if that replay is still tied, the winner is settled by a period of <a href="/wiki/Overtime_(sports)" title="Overtime (sports)">extra time</a>, and if still necessary, a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shootout</a>. Since <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_FA_Cup" title="2016–17 FA Cup">2016–17</a>, ties have been settled on the day from the quarter-finals onwards, using extra time and penalties. From <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_FA_Cup" title="2018–19 FA Cup">2018–19</a>, Fifth Round ties are also settled by extra time and penalties.
</p><p>Until <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_FA_Cup" title="1990–91 FA Cup">1990–91</a>, further replays would be played until one team was victorious. Some ties took as many as six matches to settle; in their 1975 campaign, <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> played a total of 12 games over six rounds, which remains the most games played by a team to reach a final.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Replays were traditionally played three or four days after the original game, but from <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_FA_Cup" title="1991–92 FA Cup">1991–92</a> they were staged at least 10 days later on police advice for the rounds proper. This led to <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalty shoot-outs</a> being introduced, the first of which came on 26 November 1991 when <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a> eliminated <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From <a href="/wiki/1980%E2%80%9381_FA_Cup" title="1980–81 FA Cup">1980–81</a> to <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_FA_Cup" title="1998–99 FA Cup">1998–99</a>, the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_semi-finals" title="FA Cup semi-finals">semi-finals</a> went to extra time on the day if the score after 90 minutes was a draw. If the score was still level after extra time, the match would go to a replay. Replays for the semi-finals were scrapped for <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_FA_Cup" title="1999–2000 FA Cup">1999–2000</a>, the last semi-final to go into a replay was in 1998–99 when Manchester United beat Arsenal 2–1 after extra time. The first game had ended in a 0–0 draw.
</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a> to go to extra time and a replay was the <a href="/wiki/1875_FA_Cup_Final" title="1875 FA Cup Final">1875 final</a>, between the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Engineers_A.F.C." title="Royal Engineers A.F.C.">Royal Engineers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Old_Etonians_F.C." title="Old Etonians F.C.">Old Etonians</a>. The initial tie finished 1–1 but the Royal Engineers won the replay 2–0 in normal time. The last replayed final was the <a href="/wiki/1993_FA_Cup_Final" title="1993 FA Cup Final">1993 FA Cup Final</a>, when Arsenal and <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a> fought a 1–1 draw. The replay saw Arsenal win the FA Cup, 2–1 after extra time.
</p><p>The last quarter-final to go to a replay was Manchester United vs <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_FA_Cup" title="2015–16 FA Cup">2015–16 FA Cup</a>. The original game at Old Trafford ended in a 1–1 draw, while Manchester United won the replay at the <a href="/wiki/Boleyn_Ground" title="Boleyn Ground">Boleyn Ground</a>, 2–1. It was also the last FA Cup game ever played at the Boleyn Ground.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualification_for_subsequent_competitions">Qualification for subsequent competitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Qualification for subsequent competitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_football">European football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: European football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The FA Cup winners qualify for the following season's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> (formerly named the UEFA Cup; from its launch in 1960 until 1998, they entered the now-defunct <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners&#39; Cup">UEFA Cup Winners' Cup</a> instead). This European place applies even if the team is relegated or is not in the English top flight. In the past, if the FA Cup winning team also qualified for the following season's <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> or Europa League through their league or European performance, then the losing FA Cup finalist were given the European berth of the League Cup winners and the League Cup winners will be given the league berth instead (in the Cup Winners' Cup era, teams qualifying for the UEFA Cup via other competitions will be promoted to the Cup Winners' Cup instead). FA Cup winners enter the Europa League at the group stage. Losing finalists, if they haven't qualified for Europe via the league, began earlier, at the play-off or third qualifying round stage.<sup id="cite_ref-BBCUP_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCUP-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> From the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2015–16 UEFA Europa League">2015–16 UEFA Europa League</a> season, however, <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> does not allow the runners-up to qualify for the Europa League through the competition.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> If the winner — and until 2015, the runner-up —
has already qualified for Europe through their league position (with the exception of the UEFA Cup until 1998), the FA Cup berth is then given to the highest-place team in the league who has not yet qualified.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FA_Community_Shield">FA Community Shield</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: FA Community Shield">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The FA Cup winners also qualify for the following season's single-match <a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">FA Community Shield</a>, the traditional season opener played against the previous season's <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> champions (or the Premier League runners-up if the FA Cup winners also won the league – the <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)#England" title="Double (association football)">double</a>).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_mai_2007_040.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/England_mai_2007_040.jpg/220px-England_mai_2007_040.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/England_mai_2007_040.jpg/330px-England_mai_2007_040.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/England_mai_2007_040.jpg/440px-England_mai_2007_040.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_mai_2007_040.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Since 2007 the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a> has been held at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>, on the site of <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">the previous stadium</a> which hosted it from 1923 to 2000.</div></div></div>
<p>Fixtures in the 12 rounds of the competition are usually played at the home ground of one of the two teams. The <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_semi-finals" title="FA Cup semi-finals">semi-finals</a> and <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">final</a> are played at a neutral venue – the rebuilt <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> (since <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_FA_Cup" title="2007–08 FA Cup">2008</a> and <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_FA_Cup" title="2006–07 FA Cup">2007</a> respectively).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Competition_rounds">Competition rounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Competition rounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the matches for the twelve competition rounds, the team who plays at home is decided when the fixtures are drawn – simply the first team drawn out for each fixture. Occasionally games may have to be moved to other grounds due to other events taking place, security reasons or a ground not being suitable to host popular teams. In the event of a <a href="/wiki/Draw_(tie)" class="mw-redirect" title="Draw (tie)">draw</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Replay_(sports)" title="Replay (sports)">replay</a> is played at the ground of the team who originally played <a href="/wiki/Home_advantage" title="Home advantage">away from home</a>.
</p><p>In the days when multiple replays were possible, the second replay (and any further replays) were played at neutral grounds. The clubs involved could alternatively agree to toss for home advantage in the second replay.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Semi-finals">Semi-finals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Semi-finals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The semi-finals have been played exclusively at the rebuilt <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> since <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_FA_Cup" title="2007–08 FA Cup">2008</a>, one year after it opened and after it had already hosted a final (in 2007). For the first decade of the competition, the <a href="/wiki/The_Oval" title="The Oval">Kennington Oval</a> was used as the semi-final venue. In the period between this first decade and the reopening of Wembley, semi-finals were played at high-capacity neutral venues around England; usually the home grounds of teams not involved in that semi-final, chosen to be roughly equidistant between the two teams for fairness of travel. The top three most used venues in this period were <a href="/wiki/Villa_Park" title="Villa Park">Villa Park</a> in Birmingham (55 times), <a href="/wiki/Hillsborough_Stadium" title="Hillsborough Stadium">Hillsborough</a> in Sheffield (34 times) and <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> in Manchester (23 times). The <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">original Wembley Stadium</a> was also used seven times for semi-final, between 1991 and 2000 (the last held there), but not always for fixtures featuring London teams. In 2005, both were held at the Millennium Stadium.
</p><p>In 2003 the FA took the decision to permanently use the new Wembley for semi-finals to recoup debts in financing the new stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> This was controversial, with the move seen as both unfair to fans of teams located far from London, as well as taking some of the prestige away from a Wembley final.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In defending the move, the FA has also cited the extra capacity Wembley offers, although the 2013 fixture between Millwall and Wigan led to the unprecedented step of placing 6,000 tickets on sale to neutral fans after the game failed to sell out.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> A fan poll by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> in 2013 found 86% opposition to Wembley semi-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final">Final</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Final">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The final has been played at the rebuilt <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a> since it opened, in <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_FA_Cup" title="2006–07 FA Cup">2007.</a><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The rebuilding process meant that between 2001 and 2006 they were hosted at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a> in Wales. Prior to rebuilding, the final was hosted by the <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">original Wembley Stadium</a> since it opened in <a href="/wiki/1922%E2%80%9323_FA_Cup" title="1922–23 FA Cup">1923</a> (being originally named the Empire Stadium). One exception to this 78 year series of Empire Stadium finals (including five replays) was the <a href="/wiki/1970_FA_Cup_Final" title="1970 FA Cup Final">1970 replay</a> between Leeds and Chelsea, held at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> in Manchester.
</p><p>In the 51 years prior to the Empire Stadium opening, the final (including 8 replays) was held in a variety of locations, predominantly in London, and mainly at the <a href="/wiki/The_Oval" title="The Oval">Kennington Oval</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_National_Sports_Centre#Crystal_Palace_FA_Cup_Finals_1895–1914" title="Crystal Palace National Sports Centre">Crystal Palace</a>. It was played 22 times at The Oval (the inaugural competition in 1872, and then all but two times until 1892). After The Oval, Crystal Palace hosted 21 finals from 1895 to 1914, broken up by four replays elsewhere. The other London venues were <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Bridge_(stadium)" title="Stamford Bridge (stadium)">Stamford Bridge</a> from 1920 to 1922 (the last three finals before the move to Empire Stadium); and the University of Oxford's <a href="/wiki/Lillie_Bridge_Grounds" title="Lillie Bridge Grounds">Lillie Bridge</a> in <a href="/wiki/Fulham" title="Fulham">Fulham</a> for the second ever final, in 1873. The other venues used sparingly in this period were all outside of London, as follows:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/County_Cricket_Ground,_Derby" title="County Cricket Ground, Derby">Racecourse Ground,</a> Derby (1886)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fallowfield_Stadium" title="Fallowfield Stadium">Fallowfield Stadium</a>, Manchester (1893)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Goodison_Park" title="Goodison Park">Goodison Park</a>, Liverpool (1894)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Burnden_Park" title="Burnden Park">Burnden Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolton" title="Bolton">Bolton</a> (1901 replay)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a>, Manchester (1911 replay)</li>
<li>Goodison Park (1910 replay)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a>, Sheffield (1912 replay)</li>
<li>Old Trafford (1915)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artificial_turf">Artificial turf</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Artificial turf">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The FA permitted <a href="/wiki/Artificial_turf" title="Artificial turf">artificial turf</a> (3G) pitches in all rounds of the competition from the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_FA_Cup" title="2014–15 FA Cup">2014–15 edition</a> and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Under the 2015–16 rules, the pitch must be of FIFA One Star quality, or Two Star for ties if they involve one of the 92 professional clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> This followed approval two years previously for their use in the qualifying rounds only – if a team with a 3G pitch progressed to the competition proper, they had to switch their tie to the ground of another eligible entrant with a natural grass pitch.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Having been strong proponents of the surface, the first match in the proper rounds to be played on a 3G surface was a televised first round replay at Maidstone United's <a href="/wiki/Gallagher_Stadium" title="Gallagher Stadium">Gallagher Stadium</a> on 20 November 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trophy">Trophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Trophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The eventual winners of the competition receive the FA Cup; it is only loaned to the club by the FA, under the current (2015–16) rules it must be returned by 1 March, or earlier if given seven days’ notice.<sup id="cite_ref-:12_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Traditionally, the holders had the Cup until the following year's presentation, although more recently the trophy has been taken on publicity tours by the FA in between finals.<sup id="cite_ref-recast_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recast-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_King_George_V_presents_the_FA_Cup_1914.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_King_George_V_presents_the_FA_Cup_1914.jpg/250px-The_King_George_V_presents_the_FA_Cup_1914.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_King_George_V_presents_the_FA_Cup_1914.jpg/375px-The_King_George_V_presents_the_FA_Cup_1914.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/The_King_George_V_presents_the_FA_Cup_1914.jpg/500px-The_King_George_V_presents_the_FA_Cup_1914.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2134" data-file-height="1158" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_King_George_V_presents_the_FA_Cup_1914.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>King <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a> presents the FA Cup trophy to <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Boyle_(footballer,_born_1886)" title="Tommy Boyle (footballer, born 1886)">Tommy Boyle</a> of <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley F.C.</a>, April 1914</div></div></div>
<p>The trophy comes in three parts – the cup itself, plus a lid and a base. There have been two designs of trophy in use, but five physical trophies have been presented. The original trophy, known as the "little tin idol", was 18 inches high and made by Martin, Hall &amp; Co. It was stolen in 1895 and never recovered, and so was replaced by an exact replica, used until 1910. The FA decided to change the design after the 1909 winners, Manchester United, made their own replica, leading the FA to realise they did not own the copyright.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> This new, larger design was by <a href="/wiki/Fattorini_and_Sons" title="Fattorini and Sons">Fattorini and Sons</a>, and was used from 1911.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In order to preserve this original, from 1992 it was replaced by an exact replica, although this had to be replaced after just over two decades, after showing wear and tear from being handled more than in previous eras. This third replica, first used in 2014, was built heavier to withstand the increased handling.<sup id="cite_ref-recast_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recast-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Of the four surviving trophies, only the 1895 replica has entered private ownership.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The name of the winning team is engraved on the silver band around the base as soon as the final has finished, in order to be ready in time for the presentation ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-recast_27-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recast-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> This means the engraver has just five minutes to perform a task which would take 20 under normal conditions, although time is saved by engraving the year on during the match, and sketching the presumed winner.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> During the final, the trophy is decorated with ribbons in the colours of both finalists, with the loser's ribbons being removed at the end of the game.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The tradition of tying ribbons started after <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> won the <a href="/wiki/1901_FA_Cup_Final" title="1901 FA Cup Final">1901 FA Cup Final</a> and the wife of a Spurs director decided to tie blue and white ribbons to the handles of the cup.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Traditionally, at Wembley finals, the presentation is made at the Royal Box, with players, led by the captain, mounting a staircase to a gangway in front of the box and returning by a second staircase on the other side of the box. At Cardiff the presentation was made on a podium on the pitch.
</p><p>The tradition of presenting the trophy immediately after the game did not start until the <a href="/wiki/1882_FA_Cup_Final" title="1882 FA Cup Final">1882 final</a>; after the first final in 1872 the trophy was not presented to the winners, Wanderers, until a reception held four weeks later in the Pall Mall Restaurant in London.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Under the original rules, the trophy was to be permanently presented to any club which won the competition three times, although when inaugural winners Wanderers achieved this feat by the <a href="/wiki/1876_FA_Cup_Final" title="1876 FA Cup Final">1876 final</a>, the rules were changed by FA Secretary CW Alcock (who was also captain of Wanderers in their first victory).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth F.C.</a> have the distinction of being the football club which has held the FA Cup trophy for the longest uninterrupted period - seven years.  Portsmouth had defeated Wolverhampton Wanderers 4–1 in the 1939 FA Cup Final and were awarded the trophy as 1938-1939 FA Cup Champions. But with the outbreak of World War II in September 1939, the regular Football League and FA Cup competitions for the 1939-40 season were cancelled for the duration of the war. Portsmouth's manager <a href="/wiki/Jack_Tinn" title="Jack Tinn">Jack Tinn</a> was rumoured to have kept the FA Cup trophy 'safe under his bed' throughout the duration of the war, but this is an <a href="/wiki/Urban_myth" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban myth">urban myth</a>. Because the naval city of Portsmouth was a primary strategic military target for German Luftwaffe bombing, the FA Cup trophy was actually taken ten miles to the north of Portsmouth, to the nearby Hampshire village of <a href="/wiki/Lovedean" title="Lovedean">Lovedean</a>, and there it resided in a quaint thatched roof country pub called <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lovedeanbirdinhand.co.uk">The Bird in Hand</a></i> for the seven years of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>  After the conclusion of World War II, the FA Cup trophy was presented back to the Football Association by Portsmouth F.C. in time for the 1946 FA Cup Final.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Original_design">Original design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Original design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1871_original">1871 original</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1871 original">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The first trophy, the 'little tin idol', was made by Martin, Hall &amp; Co at a cost of £20<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> It was stolen from a <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> shoe shop window belonging to William Shillcock while held by <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> on 11 September 1895 and was never seen again. Despite a £10 reward for information, the crime was never solved. As it happened while it was in their care, the FA fined Villa £25 to pay for a replacement.
</p><p>Just over 60 years later, 80 year old career criminal Henry (Harry) James Burge claimed to have committed the theft, confessing to a newspaper, with the story being published in the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Pictorial" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunday Pictorial">Sunday Pictorial</a></i> newspaper on 23 February 1958. He claimed to have carried out the robbery with two other men, although when discrepancies with a contemporaneous report in the <i><a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Post" title="Birmingham Post">Birmingham Post</a></i> newspaper (the crime pre-dated written police reports) in his account of the means of entry and other items stolen, detectives decided there was no realistic possibility of a conviction and the case was closed. Burge claimed the cup had been melted down to make counterfeit <a href="/wiki/Half_crown_(British_coin)" title="Half crown (British coin)">half-crown</a> coins, which matched known intelligence of the time, in which stolen silver was being used to forge coins which were then laundered through <a href="/wiki/Betting_shops" class="mw-redirect" title="Betting shops">betting shops</a> at a local racecourse, although Burge had no past history of forgery in a record of 42 previous convictions for which he had spent 42 years in prison. He had been further imprisoned in 1957 for seven years for theft from cars. Released in 1961, he died in 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1895_replica">1895 replica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 1895 replica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1896_FA_Cup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/1896_FA_Cup.jpg/170px-1896_FA_Cup.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="297" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/1896_FA_Cup.jpg/255px-1896_FA_Cup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/1896_FA_Cup.jpg/340px-1896_FA_Cup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1304" data-file-height="2279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1896_FA_Cup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The second FA Cup trophy, used between 1896 and 1910.</div></div></div>
<p>After being rendered obsolete by the redesign, the 1895 replica was presented in 1910 to the FA's long-serving president <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Fitzgerald_Kinnaird,_11th_Lord_Kinnaird" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur Fitzgerald Kinnaird, 11th Lord Kinnaird">Lord Kinnaird</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Kinnaird died in 1923, and his family kept it in their possession, out of view, until putting it up for auction in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> It was sold at <a href="/wiki/Christie%27s" title="Christie&#39;s">Christie's</a> auction house on 19 May 2005 for <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">£</a>420,000 (£478,400 including auction fees and taxes).<sup id="cite_ref-:3_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The sale price set a new world record for a piece of football <a href="/wiki/Souvenir" title="Souvenir">memorabilia</a>, surpassing the £254,000 paid for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Trophy" title="FIFA World Cup Trophy">Jules Rimet World Cup Trophy</a> in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The successful bidder was <a href="/wiki/David_Gold_(businessman)" title="David Gold (businessman)">David Gold</a>, the then joint chairman of <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_City_F.C." title="Birmingham City F.C.">Birmingham City</a>; claiming the FA and government were doing nothing proactive to ensure the trophy remained in the country, Gold stated his purchase was motivated by wanting to save it for the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Accordingly, Gold presented the trophy to the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_Museum" title="National Football Museum">National Football Museum</a> in Preston on 20 April 2006, where it went on immediate public display.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> It later moved with the museum to its new location in Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_28-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In November 2012, it was ceremonially presented to <a href="/wiki/Royal_Engineers_A.F.C." title="Royal Engineers A.F.C.">Royal Engineers</a>, after they beat <a href="/wiki/Wanderers_F.C." title="Wanderers F.C.">Wanderers</a> 7–1 in a charity replay of the <a href="/wiki/1872_FA_Cup_Final" title="1872 FA Cup Final">first FA Cup final</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_design">Current design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Current design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1911_original">1911 original</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 1911 original">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The redesigned trophy first used in 1911 was larger at 61.5&#160;cm (24.2 inches) high, and was designed and manufactured by <a href="/wiki/Messers_Fattorini_and_Sons" class="mw-redirect" title="Messers Fattorini and Sons">Fattorini's of Bradford</a>, coincidentally being won by <a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_A.F.C." title="Bradford City A.F.C.">Bradford City</a> in its first outing.<sup id="cite_ref-recast_27-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recast-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:3_28-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the 27 March 2016 episode of the BBC television programme <a href="/wiki/Antiques_Roadshow" title="Antiques Roadshow">Antiques Roadshow</a>, this trophy was valued at £1 million by expert <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Dickenson" title="Alastair Dickenson">Alastair Dickenson</a>, although he suggested that, due to the design featuring depictions of grapes and vines, it may not have been specifically produced for the FA, but was instead an off-the-shelf design originally meant to be a wine or champagne cooler.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_28-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A smaller, but otherwise identical, replica was also made by Fattorini, the North Wales Coast FA Cup trophy, and is contested annually by members of that regional Association.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1992_replica">1992 replica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 1992 replica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_FA_Cup_Trophy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/The_FA_Cup_Trophy.jpg/170px-The_FA_Cup_Trophy.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/The_FA_Cup_Trophy.jpg/255px-The_FA_Cup_Trophy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/The_FA_Cup_Trophy.jpg/340px-The_FA_Cup_Trophy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_FA_Cup_Trophy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The current design of the FA Cup (1992 replica pictured)</div></div></div>
<p>The 1992 replica was made by <a href="/wiki/Toye,_Kenning_and_Spencer" class="mw-redirect" title="Toye, Kenning and Spencer">Toye, Kenning and Spencer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> A copy of this trophy was also produced, in case anything happened to the primary trophy.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_replica">2014 replica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2014 replica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The 2014 replica was made by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lyte" title="Thomas Lyte">Thomas Lyte</a>, handcrafted in sterling 925 silver over 250 hours. A weight increase for greater durability has taken it to 6.3 kilograms (14&#160;lb).<sup id="cite_ref-recast_27-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recast-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Medals">Medals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Medals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Each club in the final receives 40 winners or runners-up medals to be distributed among players, staff, and officials.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_FA_Cup_Final_banner.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/2010_FA_Cup_Final_banner.jpg/250px-2010_FA_Cup_Final_banner.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/2010_FA_Cup_Final_banner.jpg/375px-2010_FA_Cup_Final_banner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/2010_FA_Cup_Final_banner.jpg/500px-2010_FA_Cup_Final_banner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4416" data-file-height="3312" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2010_FA_Cup_Final_banner.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pre-match ceremony of <a href="/wiki/2010_FA_Cup_Final" title="2010 FA Cup Final">2010 FA Cup Final</a> showing sponsorship by <a href="/wiki/E.ON" title="E.ON">E.ON</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/English_football_sponsorship" title="English football sponsorship">English football sponsorship</a></div>
<p>Since the start of the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_FA_Cup" title="1994–95 FA Cup">1994–95 season</a>, the FA Cup has been sponsored. However, to protect the identity of the competition, the sponsored name has always included 'The FA Cup' in addition to the sponsor's name, unlike sponsorship deals for the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> where the word 'cup' is preceded by only the sponsor's name. Sponsorship deals run for four years, though – as in the case of E.ON – one-year extensions may be agreed. <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates Airline</a> is the sponsor from 2015 to 2018, renaming the competition as 'The Emirates FA Cup', unlike previous editions, which included 'The FA Cup in association with E.ON' and 'The FA Cup with Budweiser'.<sup id="cite_ref-Emirates_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Emirates-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>From 2006 to 2013, <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a> supplied match balls for all FA Cup matches. They were replaced at the start of the 2013–14 season by <a href="/wiki/Nike_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Nike Inc.">Nike</a>, who produced the competition's official match ball for five seasons. <a href="/wiki/Mitre_Sports_International" title="Mitre Sports International">Mitre</a> took over for the 2018–19 season, beginning a three-year partnership with the FA.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Records_and_statistics">Records and statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Records and statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Football_records_and_statistics_in_England" title="Football records and statistics in England">Football records and statistics in England</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Final_2">Final</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Final">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Team">Team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul><li><b>Most wins:</b> 13:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> (<a href="/wiki/1930_FA_Cup_Final" title="1930 FA Cup Final">1930</a>, <a href="/wiki/1936_FA_Cup_Final" title="1936 FA Cup Final">1936</a>, <a href="/wiki/1950_FA_Cup_Final" title="1950 FA Cup Final">1950</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971_FA_Cup_Final" title="1971 FA Cup Final">1971</a>, <a href="/wiki/1979_FA_Cup_Final" title="1979 FA Cup Final">1979</a>, <a href="/wiki/1993_FA_Cup_Final" title="1993 FA Cup Final">1993</a>, <a href="/wiki/1998_FA_Cup_Final" title="1998 FA Cup Final">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_FA_Cup_Final" title="2002 FA Cup Final">2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_FA_Cup_Final" title="2003 FA Cup Final">2003</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_FA_Cup_Final" title="2005 FA Cup Final">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Cup_Final" title="2014 FA Cup Final">2014</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_FA_Cup_Final" title="2015 FA Cup Final">2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_FA_Cup_Final" title="2017 FA Cup Final">2017</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Most consecutive wins:</b> 3, joint record:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Wanderers_F.C." title="Wanderers F.C.">Wanderers</a> (<a href="/wiki/1876_FA_Cup_Final" title="1876 FA Cup Final">1876</a>, <a href="/wiki/1877_FA_Cup_Final" title="1877 FA Cup Final">1877</a>, <a href="/wiki/1878_FA_Cup_Final" title="1878 FA Cup Final">1878</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> (<a href="/wiki/1884_FA_Cup_Final" title="1884 FA Cup Final">1884</a>, <a href="/wiki/1885_FA_Cup_Final" title="1885 FA Cup Final">1885</a>, <a href="/wiki/1886_FA_Cup_Final" title="1886 FA Cup Final">1886</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Most appearances in a final:</b> 20, joint record:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> (<a href="/wiki/1927_FA_Cup_Final" title="1927 FA Cup Final">1927</a>, <a href="/wiki/1930_FA_Cup_Final" title="1930 FA Cup Final">1930</a>, <a href="/wiki/1932_FA_Cup_Final" title="1932 FA Cup Final">1932</a>, <a href="/wiki/1936_FA_Cup_Final" title="1936 FA Cup Final">1936</a>, <a href="/wiki/1950_FA_Cup_Final" title="1950 FA Cup Final">1950</a>, <a href="/wiki/1952_FA_Cup_Final" title="1952 FA Cup Final">1952</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971_FA_Cup_Final" title="1971 FA Cup Final">1971</a>, <a href="/wiki/1972_FA_Cup_Final" title="1972 FA Cup Final">1972</a>, <a href="/wiki/1978_FA_Cup_Final" title="1978 FA Cup Final">1978</a>, <a href="/wiki/1979_FA_Cup_Final" title="1979 FA Cup Final">1979</a>, <a href="/wiki/1980_FA_Cup_Final" title="1980 FA Cup Final">1980</a>, <a href="/wiki/1993_FA_Cup_Final" title="1993 FA Cup Final">1993</a>, <a href="/wiki/1998_FA_Cup_Final" title="1998 FA Cup Final">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001_FA_Cup_Final" title="2001 FA Cup Final">2001</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_FA_Cup_Final" title="2002 FA Cup Final">2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_FA_Cup_Final" title="2003 FA Cup Final">2003</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_FA_Cup_Final" title="2005 FA Cup Final">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Cup_Final" title="2014 FA Cup Final">2014</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_FA_Cup_Final" title="2015 FA Cup Final">2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_FA_Cup_Final" title="2017 FA Cup Final">2017</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> (<a href="/wiki/1909_FA_Cup_Final" title="1909 FA Cup Final">1909</a>, <a href="/wiki/1948_FA_Cup_Final" title="1948 FA Cup Final">1948</a>, <a href="/wiki/1957_FA_Cup_Final" title="1957 FA Cup Final">1957</a>, <a href="/wiki/1958_FA_Cup_Final" title="1958 FA Cup Final">1958</a>, <a href="/wiki/1963_FA_Cup_Final" title="1963 FA Cup Final">1963</a>, <a href="/wiki/1976_FA_Cup_Final" title="1976 FA Cup Final">1976</a>, <a href="/wiki/1977_FA_Cup_Final" title="1977 FA Cup Final">1977</a>, <a href="/wiki/1979_FA_Cup_Final" title="1979 FA Cup Final">1979</a>, <a href="/wiki/1983_FA_Cup_Final" title="1983 FA Cup Final">1983</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985_FA_Cup_Final" title="1985 FA Cup Final">1985</a>, <a href="/wiki/1990_FA_Cup_Final" title="1990 FA Cup Final">1990</a>, <a href="/wiki/1994_FA_Cup_Final" title="1994 FA Cup Final">1994</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995_FA_Cup_Final" title="1995 FA Cup Final">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/1996_FA_Cup_Final" title="1996 FA Cup Final">1996</a>, <a href="/wiki/1999_FA_Cup_Final" title="1999 FA Cup Final">1999</a>, <a href="/wiki/2004_FA_Cup_Final" title="2004 FA Cup Final">2004</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_FA_Cup_Final" title="2005 FA Cup Final">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_FA_Cup_Final" title="2007 FA Cup Final">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2016_FA_Cup_Final" title="2016 FA Cup Final">2016</a>, <a href="/wiki/2018_FA_Cup_Final" title="2018 FA Cup Final">2018</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Most consecutive/uninterrupted years as FA Cup Champions</b>: 7, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth F.C.</a>, (<a href="/wiki/1939_FA_Cup_Final" title="1939 FA Cup Final">1939</a>–1946)</li>
<li><b>Most Final appearances without ever winning:</b> 4, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> (<a href="/wiki/1949_FA_Cup_Final" title="1949 FA Cup Final">1949</a>, <a href="/wiki/1961_FA_Cup_Final" title="1961 FA Cup Final">1961</a>, <a href="/wiki/1963_FA_Cup_Final" title="1963 FA Cup Final">1963</a>, <a href="/wiki/1969_FA_Cup_Final" title="1969 FA Cup Final">1969</a>)</li>
<li><b>Most Final appearances without ever losing:</b> 5, <a href="/wiki/Wanderers_F.C." title="Wanderers F.C.">Wanderers</a> (<a href="/wiki/1872_FA_Cup_Final" title="1872 FA Cup Final">1872</a>, <a href="/wiki/1873_FA_Cup_Final" title="1873 FA Cup Final">1873</a>, <a href="/wiki/1876_FA_Cup_Final" title="1876 FA Cup Final">1876</a>, <a href="/wiki/1877_FA_Cup_Final" title="1877 FA Cup Final">1877</a>, <a href="/wiki/1878_FA_Cup_Final" title="1878 FA Cup Final">1878</a>)</li>
<li><b>Most Final appearances without losing (streak):</b> 7, <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> (<a href="/wiki/1901_FA_Cup_Final" title="1901 FA Cup Final">1901</a>, <a href="/wiki/1921_FA_Cup_Final" title="1921 FA Cup Final">1921</a>, <a href="/wiki/1961_FA_Cup_Final" title="1961 FA Cup Final">1961</a>, <a href="/wiki/1962_FA_Cup_Final" title="1962 FA Cup Final">1962</a>, <a href="/wiki/1967_FA_Cup_Final" title="1967 FA Cup Final">1967</a>, <a href="/wiki/1981_FA_Cup_Final" title="1981 FA Cup Final">1981</a>, <a href="/wiki/1982_FA_Cup_Final" title="1982 FA Cup Final">1982</a>)</li>
<li><b>Longest gap between wins:</b> 69 years, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> (<a href="/wiki/1939_FA_Cup_Final" title="1939 FA Cup Final">1939</a>–<a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">2008</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Biggest win:</b> 6 goals, joint record:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bury_F.C." title="Bury F.C.">Bury</a> 6–0 <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a>, (<a href="/wiki/1903_FA_Cup_Final" title="1903 FA Cup Final">1903</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> 6–0 <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a>, (<a href="/wiki/2019_FA_Cup_Final" title="2019 FA Cup Final">2019</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Most goals in a final:</b> 7:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> 6–1 <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a> (<a href="/wiki/1890_FA_Cup_Final" title="1890 FA Cup Final">1890</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a> 4–3 <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> (<a href="/wiki/1953_FA_Cup_Final" title="1953 FA Cup Final">1953</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Most goals by a losing side:</b> 3:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a>: Lost 3–4 against <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a> (<a href="/wiki/1953_FA_Cup_Final" title="1953 FA Cup Final">1953</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>: Drew 3–3 but lost in a penalty shootout against <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> (<a href="/wiki/2006_FA_Cup_Final" title="2006 FA Cup Final">2006</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Most defeats:</b> 8, joint record:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> (<a href="/wiki/1893_FA_Cup_Final" title="1893 FA Cup Final">1893</a>, <a href="/wiki/1897_FA_Cup_Final" title="1897 FA Cup Final">1897</a>, <a href="/wiki/1907_FA_Cup_Final" title="1907 FA Cup Final">1907</a>, <a href="/wiki/1968_FA_Cup_Final" title="1968 FA Cup Final">1968</a>, <a href="/wiki/1985_FA_Cup_Final" title="1985 FA Cup Final">1985</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986_FA_Cup_Final" title="1986 FA Cup Final">1986</a>, <a href="/wiki/1989_FA_Cup_Final" title="1989 FA Cup Final">1989</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_FA_Cup_Final" title="2009 FA Cup Final">2009</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> (<a href="/wiki/1957_FA_Cup_Final" title="1957 FA Cup Final">1957</a>, <a href="/wiki/1958_FA_Cup_Final" title="1958 FA Cup Final">1958</a>, <a href="/wiki/1976_FA_Cup_Final" title="1976 FA Cup Final">1976</a>, <a href="/wiki/1979_FA_Cup_Final" title="1979 FA Cup Final">1979</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995_FA_Cup_Final" title="1995 FA Cup Final">1995</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_FA_Cup_Final" title="2005 FA Cup Final">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2007_FA_Cup_Final" title="2007 FA Cup Final">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2018_FA_Cup_Final" title="2018 FA Cup Final">2018</a>)</li></ul></li></ul>

<ul><li><b>Most wins by player:</b> 7: <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Cole" title="Ashley Cole">Ashley Cole</a> (<a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>) (<a href="/wiki/2002_FA_Cup_Final" title="2002 FA Cup Final">2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_FA_Cup_Final" title="2003 FA Cup Final">2003</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_FA_Cup_Final" title="2005 FA Cup Final">2005</a>) &amp; (<a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>) (<a href="/wiki/2007_FA_Cup_Final" title="2007 FA Cup Final">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_FA_Cup_Final" title="2009 FA Cup Final">2009</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_FA_Cup_Final" title="2010 FA Cup Final">2010</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_FA_Cup_Final" title="2012 FA Cup Final">2012</a>)</li>

<li><b>Most appearances:</b> 9, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Kinnaird,_11th_Lord_Kinnaird" title="Arthur Kinnaird, 11th Lord Kinnaird">Arthur Kinnaird</a> (<a href="/wiki/Wanderers_F.C." title="Wanderers F.C.">Wanderers</a>) (<a href="/wiki/1873_FA_Cup_Final" title="1873 FA Cup Final">1872–73</a>, <a href="/wiki/1876_FA_Cup_Final" title="1876 FA Cup Final">1875–76</a>, <a href="/wiki/1877_FA_Cup_Final" title="1877 FA Cup Final">1876–77</a>, <a href="/wiki/1878_FA_Cup_Final" title="1878 FA Cup Final">1877–78</a>) &amp; (<a href="/wiki/Old_Etonians_F.C." title="Old Etonians F.C.">Old Etonians</a>) (<a href="/wiki/1875_FA_Cup_Final" title="1875 FA Cup Final">1874–75</a>, <a href="/wiki/1879_FA_Cup_Final" title="1879 FA Cup Final">1878–79</a>, <a href="/wiki/1881_FA_Cup_Final" title="1881 FA Cup Final">1880–81</a>, <a href="/wiki/1882_FA_Cup_Final" title="1882 FA Cup Final">1881–82</a>, <a href="/wiki/1883_FA_Cup_Final" title="1883 FA Cup Final">1882–83</a>)</li>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Billy_Townley" class="mw-redirect" title="Billy Townley">Billy Townley</a> (<a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>) (<a href="/wiki/1890_FA_Cup_Final" title="1890 FA Cup Final">1890</a>)</li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Stan_Mortensen" title="Stan Mortensen">Stan Mortensen</a> (<a href="/wiki/Blackpool_F.C." title="Blackpool F.C.">Blackpool</a>) (<a href="/wiki/1953_FA_Cup_Final" title="1953 FA Cup Final">1953</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Most goals (all finals):</b> 5, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Rush" title="Ian Rush">Ian Rush</a> (<a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>) (2 in <a href="/wiki/1986_FA_Cup_Final" title="1986 FA Cup Final">1986</a>, 2 in <a href="/wiki/1989_FA_Cup_Final" title="1989 FA Cup Final">1989</a>, 1 in <a href="/wiki/1992_FA_Cup_Final" title="1992 FA Cup Final">1992</a>)</li>
<li><b>Most finals scored in:</b> 4, <a href="/wiki/Didier_Drogba" title="Didier Drogba">Didier Drogba</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>) (1 each in <a href="/wiki/2007_FA_Cup_Final" title="2007 FA Cup Final">2007</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_FA_Cup_Final" title="2009 FA Cup Final">2009</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_FA_Cup_Final" title="2010 FA Cup Final">2010</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_FA_Cup_Final" title="2012 FA Cup Final">2012</a>)</li>
<li><b>Youngest FA Cup finalist:</b> <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Weston" title="Curtis Weston">Curtis Weston</a> (<a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a>), 17 years and 119 days (<a href="/wiki/2004_FA_Cup_Final" title="2004 FA Cup Final">2004</a>)</li>
<li><b>Youngest player to score in an FA Cup Final:</b> <a href="/wiki/Norman_Whiteside" title="Norman Whiteside">Norman Whiteside</a> (<a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>), 18 years and 19 days (<a href="/wiki/1983_FA_Cup_Final" title="1983 FA Cup Final">1983</a>)</li>
<li><b>Oldest player:</b> <a href="/wiki/Billy_Hampson" title="Billy Hampson">Billy Hampson</a> (<a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>), 41 years and 257 days (<a href="/wiki/1924_FA_Cup_Final" title="1924 FA Cup Final">1924</a>)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="All_rounds">All rounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: All rounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><b>Biggest win:</b> <a href="/wiki/Preston_North_End_F.C." title="Preston North End F.C.">Preston North End</a> 26–0 <a href="/wiki/Hyde_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Hyde F.C.">Hyde</a> (<a href="/wiki/1887%E2%80%9388_FA_Cup#First_round" title="1887–88 FA Cup">First Round, 15 October 1887</a>)</li>

<li><b>Highest attendance at Wembley:</b> 126,047 (official) up to 300,000 (estimate) at the "<a href="/wiki/1923_FA_Cup_Final" title="1923 FA Cup Final">White Horse Final</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> <i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>, 28 April 1923)</li>
<li><b>Most clubs competing for trophy in a season:</b> 763 (<a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_FA_Cup" title="2011–12 FA Cup">2011–12</a>)</li>

<li><b>Longest penalty shootout:</b> 20 penalties each, <a href="/wiki/Tunbridge_Wells_F.C." title="Tunbridge Wells F.C.">Tunbridge Wells</a> <i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/Littlehampton_Town_F.C." title="Littlehampton Town F.C.">Littlehampton Town</a> (<a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_FA_Cup#FA_Cup_Qualifying_Rounds#Replays" title="2005–06 FA Cup">Preliminary Round Replay, 31 August 2005</a>; Tunbridge Wells won 16–15)</li>
<li><b>Most rounds played in a season:</b> 9, for:
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Brighton_%26_Hove_Albion_F.C." title="Brighton &amp; Hove Albion F.C.">Brighton &amp; Hove Albion</a> (<a href="/wiki/1932%E2%80%9333_FA_Cup" title="1932–33 FA Cup">1932–33</a>: 1st–4th Qualifying Rounds, 1st–5th Rounds)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_Brighton_A.F.C." title="New Brighton A.F.C.">New Brighton</a> (<a href="/wiki/1956%E2%80%9357_FA_Cup" title="1956–57 FA Cup">1956–57</a>: Preliminary, 1st–4th Qualifying Rounds, 1st–4th Rounds)</li>
