<li><a href="/wiki/Harlow_Town_F.C." title="Harlow Town F.C.">Harlow Town</a> (<a href="/wiki/1979%E2%80%9380_FA_Cup" title="1979–80 FA Cup">1979–80</a>: Preliminary, 1st–4th Qualifying Rounds, 1st–4th Rounds)</li></ul></li>
<li><b>Most games played in a season:</b> 13, <a href="/wiki/Bideford_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Bideford F.C.">Bideford</a> (<a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%9374_FA_Cup" title="1973–74 FA Cup">1973–74</a>: one First Qualifying, two Second Qualifying, five Third Qualifying, four Fourth Qualifying and one First Round)</li>
<li><b>Fastest goal:</b> 4 seconds, Gareth Morris (for <a href="/wiki/Ashton_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashton United">Ashton United</a> <i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/Skelmersdale_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Skelmersdale United">Skelmersdale United</a>, <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_FA_Cup_Qualifying_Rounds#1st_Qualifying_Round" class="mw-redirect" title="2001–02 FA Cup Qualifying Rounds">1st Qualifying Round, 17 September 2001</a>)</li>
<li><b>Most consecutive games without defeat:</b> 22, <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> (<a href="/wiki/1884%E2%80%9385_FA_Cup#First_Round" title="1884–85 FA Cup">First Round, 1884</a> through <a href="/wiki/1886%E2%80%9387_FA_Cup#Second_round" title="1886–87 FA Cup">Second round, replay, 1886</a>. Won two FA Cups.)</li>
<li><b>Most consecutive games without defeat:</b> (Excluding defeat by penalty shoot-out) 29, <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> (<a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_FA_Cup#Third_Round_Proper" title="2008–09 FA Cup">Third Round Proper, 2009</a> through <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_FA_Cup#Fourth_round_proper" title="2012–13 FA Cup">Fourth Round Proper, replay, 2013</a>. Won three FA Cups.)</li>
<li><b>Fastest hat-trick:</b> 2 min 20 sec, <a href="/wiki/Nantwich_Town_F.C." title="Nantwich Town F.C.">Andy Locke</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Nantwich_Town_F.C." title="Nantwich Town F.C.">Nantwich Town</a> <i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/Droylsden_F.C." title="Droylsden F.C.">Droylsden</a>, <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_FA_Cup_Qualifying_Rounds#Preliminary_Round" class="mw-redirect" title="1995–96 FA Cup Qualifying Rounds">Preliminary Round, August 1995</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Most career goals:</b> 49, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Cursham" title="Harry Cursham">Harry Cursham</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a> in 12 tournaments from <a href="/wiki/1877%E2%80%9378_FA_Cup" title="1877–78 FA Cup">1877–78</a> to <a href="/wiki/1888%E2%80%9389_FA_Cup_Qualifying_Rounds" class="mw-redirect" title="1888–89 FA Cup Qualifying Rounds">1888–89</a>).</li>
<li><b>Most goals by a player in a single FA Cup season:</b> 19, <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Ross_(footballer,_born_1866)" title="Jimmy Ross (footballer, born 1866)">Jimmy Ross</a> (for <a href="/wiki/Preston_North_End_F.C." title="Preston North End F.C.">Preston North End</a>, <a href="/wiki/1887%E2%80%9388_FA_Cup" title="1887–88 FA Cup">1887–88</a>. Preston outscored opponents 50–5 over 7 matches, including "Biggest win" shown above.).<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Most goals by a player in a single FA Cup game:</b> 9, <a href="/wiki/Ted_MacDougall" title="Ted MacDougall">Ted MacDougall</a> (for <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">AFC Bournemouth</a> in 11–0 defeat of <a href="/wiki/Margate_F.C." title="Margate F.C.">Margate</a>, <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_FA_Cup#First_Round_Proper" title="1971–72 FA Cup">First Round Proper, 20 November 1971</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Player who scored in every round in a single FA Cup season:</b> Peter Osgood, Chelsea, 1969- 70.</li>
<li><b>Scoreline:</b> Two examples of teams scoring 7 goals and not winning – <a href="/wiki/Dulwich_Hamlet_F.C." title="Dulwich Hamlet F.C.">Dulwich Hamlet</a> 8–7 <a href="/wiki/St_Albans_City_F.C." title="St Albans City F.C.">St Albans City</a> (<a href="/wiki/1922%E2%80%9323_FA_Cup#Calendar" title="1922–23 FA Cup">Fourth Qualifying Round Replay, 22 November 1922</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Dulwich_Hamlet_F.C." title="Dulwich Hamlet F.C.">Dulwich Hamlet</a> 7–7 <a href="/wiki/Wealdstone_F.C." title="Wealdstone F.C.">Wealdstone</a> (<a href="/wiki/1929%E2%80%9330_FA_Cup#Calendar" title="1929–30 FA Cup">Fourth Qualifying Round, 16 November 1929</a>).</li>
<li><b>Youngest player:</b> <a href="/wiki/Andy_Awford" title="Andy Awford">Andy Awford</a>, 15 years and 88 days (for <a href="/wiki/Worcester_City_F.C." title="Worcester City F.C.">Worcester City</a> <i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/Boreham_Wood_F.C." title="Boreham Wood F.C.">Boreham Wood</a>, <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_FA_Cup_Qualifying_Rounds#3rd_Qualifying_Round" class="mw-redirect" title="1987–88 FA Cup Qualifying Rounds">3rd Qualifying Round, 10 October 1987</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Youngest goalscorer:</b> <a href="/wiki/Barrow_Town_F.C.#History" title="Barrow Town F.C.">Sean Cato</a>, 16 years and 25 days (for <a href="/wiki/Barrow_Town_F.C." title="Barrow Town F.C.">Barrow Town</a> <i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/Rothwell_Town_F.C." title="Rothwell Town F.C.">Rothwell Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_FA_Cup_qualifying_rounds#Preliminary_Round" title="2011–12 FA Cup qualifying rounds">Preliminary Round, 3 September 2011</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><b>Youngest goalscorer (proper rounds):</b> <a href="/wiki/George_Williams_(footballer,_born_1995)" title="George Williams (footballer, born 1995)">George Williams</a>, 16 years and 66 days (for <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Dons_F.C." title="Milton Keynes Dons F.C.">Milton Keynes Dons</a> <i>v.</i> <a href="/wiki/Nantwich_Town_F.C." title="Nantwich Town F.C.">Nantwich Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_FA_Cup#First_round_proper" title="2011–12 FA Cup">First Round Proper, 12 November 2011</a>)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cup_runs_and_giant_killings">Cup runs and giant killings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cup runs and giant killings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The possibility of unlikely victories in the earlier rounds of the competition, where lower ranked teams beat higher placed opposition in what is known as a "giant killing" or "cupset", is much anticipated by the public. Such upsets are considered an integral part of the tradition and prestige of the competition, and the attention gained by giant-killing teams can be as great as that for winners of the cup.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Almost every club in the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">League Pyramid</a> has a fondly remembered giant-killing act in its history.<sup id="cite_ref-times_analysis_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times_analysis-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> It is considered particularly newsworthy when a top <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> team suffers an upset defeat, or where the giant-killer is a non-league club, i.e. from outside the professional levels of <a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">The Football League</a>.
</p><p>One analysis of four years of FA Cup results showed that it was 99.85 per cent likely that at least one team would beat one from its next higher division in a given year. The probability drops to 48.8 per cent for a two-division gap, and 39.28 per cent for a three-division gap.<sup id="cite_ref-times_analysis_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times_analysis-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Football League">The Football League</a> was founded in 1888, 16 years after the first FA Cup competition. Since the creation of The Football League, <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> is the only non-league "giant-killer" to win the Cup, taking the <a href="/wiki/1901_FA_Cup_Final" title="1901 FA Cup Final">1901 FA Cup</a> with a victory over <a href="/wiki/1899%E2%80%931900_Football_League" title="1899–1900 Football League">reigning</a> league runners-up <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a>: although at that time, there were only two divisions and 36 clubs in the Football League, and Spurs were champions of the next strongest football league – the Southern League and probably already good enough for the First Division (as was shown when they joined the Second Division in 1908 and immediately won promotion to the First.) Only two other actual non-League clubs have even reached the final since the founding of the League: Sheffield Wednesday in 1890 (champions of the Football Alliance, a rival league which was already effectively the Second Division, which it formally became in 1892 – Wednesday being let straight into the First Division), and <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> in 1900 and 1902 (in which years they were also Southern League champions, proving the strength of that league: again, they were probably of equivalent standard to a First Division club at the time, but Southampton's form subsequently faded and they did not join the League till 1920 and the formation of the Third Division.)
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-league_giant_killings">Non-league giant killings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Non-league giant killings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The most recent examples of a <a href="/wiki/Non-league" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-league">non-league</a> team (<a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system#The_System" title="English football league system">Levels 5 to 10</a>) beating a Level 1 opponent are <a href="/wiki/National_League_(division)" title="National League (division)">National League</a> side <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_City_F.C." title="Lincoln City F.C.">Lincoln City</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Burnley_0%E2%80%931_Lincoln_City_(2017)" class="mw-redirect" title="Burnley 0–1 Lincoln City (2017)">away victory</a> over Premier League side <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_FA_Cup" title="2016–17 FA Cup">2016–17 FA Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Conference_Premier" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference Premier">Conference Premier</a> side <a href="/wiki/Luton_Town_F.C." title="Luton Town F.C.">Luton Town</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_0%E2%80%931_Luton_Town_(2013)" title="Norwich City 0–1 Luton Town (2013)">away victory</a> over Level 1 <a href="/wiki/English_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="English Premier League">Premier League</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_FA_Cup#Fourth_Round_Proper" title="2012–13 FA Cup">2012–13 Fourth Round Proper</a>. Prior to that game, the last time a non-league side defeated a Level 1 club was in 1989 when <a href="/wiki/Sutton_United_F.C." title="Sutton United F.C.">Sutton United</a> claimed a <a href="/wiki/Sutton_United_2%E2%80%931_Coventry_City_(1989)" title="Sutton United 2–1 Coventry City (1989)">2–1 victory</a> at home over <a href="/wiki/Coventry_City_F.C." title="Coventry City F.C.">Coventry City</a>, who had won the FA Cup less than two years prior.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_FA_Cup" title="1971–72 FA Cup">1971–72 FA Cup</a>, a non-league side achieved a Level 1 giant killing that was voted "best FA Cup tie ever" in a 2007 poll by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Non-league <a href="/wiki/Hereford_United_F.C." title="Hereford United F.C.">Hereford United</a> was trailing First Division <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> 0–1 with less than seven minutes left in the <a href="/wiki/1971%E2%80%9372_FA_Cup#Third_Round_Proper" title="1971–72 FA Cup">Third Round Proper replay</a>, when Hereford's Ronnie Radford scored the equalizer – a goal still shown regularly when FA Cup fixtures are broadcast. Hereford finished the shocking comeback by defeating Newcastle 2–1 in the match.
</p><p>Some small clubs gain a reputation for being "cup specialists" after two or more giant killing feats within a few years.<sup id="cite_ref-times_analysis_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-times_analysis-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yeovil_Town_F.C." title="Yeovil Town F.C.">Yeovil Town</a> holds the record for the most victories over league opposition as a non-league team, having recorded 20 wins through the years before it achieved <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation#English_example" title="Promotion and relegation">promotion</a> into The Football League.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The record for a club which has never entered The Football League is held by <a href="/wiki/Altrincham_F.C." title="Altrincham F.C.">Altrincham</a>, with 17 wins against league teams.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-league_cup_runs">Non-league cup runs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Non-league cup runs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_non-league_clubs_in_the_Fifth_Round_of_the_FA_Cup_since_1945" class="mw-redirect" title="List of non-league clubs in the Fifth Round of the FA Cup since 1945">List of non-league clubs in the Fifth Round of the FA Cup since 1945</a></div>
<p>For non-league teams, reaching the Third Round Proper – where all Level 1 sides now enter – is considered a major achievement. In the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_FA_Cup" title="2008–09 FA Cup">2008–09 FA Cup</a>, a record nine non-league teams achieved this feat.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> As of the 2016–17 season, only nine non-league teams have <a href="/wiki/List_of_non-league_clubs_in_the_Fifth_Round_of_the_FA_Cup_since_1945" class="mw-redirect" title="List of non-league clubs in the Fifth Round of the FA Cup since 1945">reached the Fifth Round Proper</a> (final 16) since 1945,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and only <a href="/wiki/Lincoln_City_F.C." title="Lincoln City F.C.">Lincoln City</a> have progressed to the Sixth Round (final 8), during the 2016–17 edition of the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chasetown_F.C." title="Chasetown F.C.">Chasetown</a>, while playing at <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system#The_system" title="English football league system">Level 8</a> of English football during the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_FA_Cup" title="2007–08 FA Cup">2007–08 competition</a>, are the lowest-ranked team to ever play in the Third Round Proper (final 64, of 731 teams entered that season). Chasetown was then a member of the <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Southern_Football_League" title="2007–08 Southern Football League">Southern League Division One Midlands</a> (a lower level within the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League" title="Southern Football League">Southern Football League</a>), when they lost to <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Championship">Football League Championship</a> (Level 2) team <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>, the eventual FA Cup runners-up that year.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Their success earned the lowly organisation over £60,000 in prize money.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Giant_killings_between_League_clubs">Giant killings between League clubs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Giant killings between League clubs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In games between League sides, one of the most notable results was the <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_A.F.C._2%E2%80%931_Arsenal_F.C." title="Wrexham A.F.C. 2–1 Arsenal F.C.">1992 victory</a> by <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Wrexham F.C.">Wrexham</a>, <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Football_League#Fourth_Division" title="1990–91 Football League">bottom</a> of the previous season's League (avoiding relegation due to expansion of <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">The Football League</a>), over <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_Football_League#First_Division" title="1990–91 Football League">reigning</a> champions Arsenal. Another similar shock was when <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_Town_F.C." title="Shrewsbury Town F.C.">Shrewsbury Town</a> beat <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> 2–1 in 2003. Everton finished 7th in the Premier League and Shrewsbury Town were relegated to the Football Conference that same season.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Winners_and_finalists">Winners and finalists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Winners and finalists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_FA_Cup_Finals" title="List of FA Cup Finals">List of FA Cup Finals</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Results_by_team">Results by team</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Results by team">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since its establishment, the FA Cup has been won by 43 different teams. Teams shown in <i>italics</i> are no longer in existence. Additionally, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_F.C." title="Queen&#39;s Park F.C.">Queen's Park</a> ceased to be eligible to enter the FA Cup after a <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Football_Association" title="Scottish Football Association">Scottish Football Association</a> ruling in 1887.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

</li>
</ol></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consecutive_winners">Consecutive winners</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Consecutive winners">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Four clubs have won consecutive FA Cups on more than one occasion: <a href="/wiki/Wanderers_F.C." title="Wanderers F.C.">Wanderers</a> (1872, 1873 and 1876, 1877, 1878), <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a> (1884, 1885, 1886 and 1890, 1891), <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> (1961, 1962 and 1981, 1982) and <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> (<a href="/wiki/2002_FA_Cup_Final" title="2002 FA Cup Final">2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_FA_Cup_Final" title="2003 FA Cup Final">2003</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Cup_Final" title="2014 FA Cup Final">2014</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_FA_Cup_Final" title="2015 FA Cup Final">2015</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Winning_managers">Winning managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Winning managers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_FA_Cup_winning_managers" title="List of FA Cup winning managers">List of FA Cup winning managers</a></div>
<p>The record for most winner's medals for a manager is held by <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a>, who has won seven titles with Arsenal (<a href="/wiki/1998_FA_Cup_Final" title="1998 FA Cup Final">1998</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_FA_Cup_Final" title="2002 FA Cup Final">2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003_FA_Cup_Final" title="2003 FA Cup Final">2003</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_FA_Cup_Final" title="2005 FA Cup Final">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_FA_Cup_Final" title="2014 FA Cup Final">2014</a>, <a href="/wiki/2015_FA_Cup_Final" title="2015 FA Cup Final">2015</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_FA_Cup_Final" title="2017 FA Cup Final">2017</a>).
</p>
<h3><span id="Doubles.2FTrebles"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Doubles/Trebles">Doubles/Trebles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Doubles/Trebles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a> (2019) are the only club to have achieved a domestic <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">League and Cup treble</a>, having beaten <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> 4-3 on penalties in the <a href="/wiki/2019_EFL_Cup_Final" title="2019 EFL Cup Final">EFL Cup Final</a>, finished at the top of the English <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>, and beaten <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> 6-0 in the FA Cup Final. Seven clubs have won the FA Cup as part of a <a href="/wiki/Double_(association_football)" title="Double (association football)">League and Cup double</a>, namely <a href="/wiki/Preston_North_End_F.C." title="Preston North End F.C.">Preston North End</a> (1889), <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> (1897), <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> (1961), <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> (1971, 1998, 2002), <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> (1986), <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> (1994, 1996, 1999) and <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> (2010). In 1993, Arsenal became the first side to win both the FA Cup and the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> in the same season when they beat <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a> 2–1 in both finals. Liverpool (in 2001) and Chelsea (in 2007) have since repeated this feat. In 2012, Chelsea accomplished a different cup double consisting of the FA Cup and the <a href="/wiki/2012_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2012 UEFA Champions League Final">2012</a> <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a>. In <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_in_English_football" title="1998–99 in English football">1998–99</a>, Manchester United added the <a href="/wiki/1999_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="1999 UEFA Champions League Final">1999</a> <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> title to their league and cup double to complete a unique <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)" title="Treble (association football)">Treble</a>. Two years later, in <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_in_English_football" title="2000–01 in English football">2000–01</a>, Liverpool won the FA Cup, <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> to complete a <a href="/wiki/Treble_(association_football)#Other_trebles" title="Treble (association football)">cup treble</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_England">Outside England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Outside England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The FA Cup has only been won by a non-English team once. <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> achieved this in 1927 when they beat Arsenal in the final at Wembley. They had previously made it to the final only to lose to <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> in 1925 and lost another final to <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> in 2008. Cardiff City is also the only team to win the national cups of two different countries in the same season, having also won the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Cup" title="Welsh Cup">Welsh Cup</a> in 1927. The Scottish team <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_F.C." title="Queen&#39;s Park F.C.">Queen's Park</a> reached and lost the final in both 1884 and 1885.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Outside_the_top_division">Outside the top division</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Outside the top division">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the creation of the Football League in 1888, the final has never been contested by two teams from outside the top division, and there have only been eight winners who were not in the top flight: <a href="/wiki/Notts_County_F.C." title="Notts County F.C.">Notts County</a> (<a href="/wiki/1894_FA_Cup_Final" title="1894 FA Cup Final">1894</a>); <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> (<a href="/wiki/1901_FA_Cup_Final" title="1901 FA Cup Final">1901</a>); <a href="/wiki/Wolverhampton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wolverhampton Wanderers F.C.">Wolverhampton Wanderers</a> (<a href="/wiki/1908_FA_Cup_Final" title="1908 FA Cup Final">1908</a>); <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a> (<a href="/wiki/1912_FA_Cup_Final" title="1912 FA Cup Final">1912</a>); <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> (<a href="/wiki/1931_FA_Cup_Final" title="1931 FA Cup Final">1931</a>); <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a> (<a href="/wiki/1973_FA_Cup_Final" title="1973 FA Cup Final">1973</a>), <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> (<a href="/wiki/1976_FA_Cup_Final" title="1976 FA Cup Final">1976</a>) and <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a> (<a href="/wiki/1980_FA_Cup_Final" title="1980 FA Cup Final">1980</a>). With the exception of Tottenham, these clubs were all playing in the second tier (the old <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Second_Division" title="Football League Second Division">Second Division</a>) – Tottenham were playing in the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League" title="Southern Football League">Southern League</a> and were only elected to the Football League in 1908, meaning they are the only non-League winners of the FA Cup since the League's creation. Other than Tottenham's victory, only <a href="#FA_Cup_winners_and_finalists">24 finalists</a> have come from outside English football's top tier, with a record of 7 wins and 17 runners-up: and none at all from the third tier or lower, Southampton (<a href="/wiki/1902_FA_Cup_Final" title="1902 FA Cup Final">1902</a>, then in the Southern League) being the last finalist from outside the top two tiers.
</p><p>Sunderland's win in 1973 was considered a major upset, having beaten <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a> who finished third in the top flight that season.,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> as was West Ham's victory over Arsenal in 1980 as the Gunners were in their third successive FA Cup Final and were also the cup holders from the previous year as well as just having finished 4th in the First Division, whereas West Ham had ended the season 7th in Division 2. This also marked the last time (as of 2018-19) a team from outside the top division won the FA cup. Uniquely, in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_FA_Cup" title="2007–08 FA Cup">2008</a> three of the four semi-finalists (Barnsley, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> and West Bromwich) were from outside the top division, although the eventual winner was the last remaining top-flight team, <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> West Bromwich (1931) are the only team to have won the FA Cup and earned promotion to the top flight in the same season; whereas <a href="/wiki/Wigan_Athletic_F.C." title="Wigan Athletic F.C.">Wigan Athletic</a> (<a href="/wiki/2013_FA_Cup_Final" title="2013 FA Cup Final">2013</a>) are the only team to have won the Cup and been relegated from the top flight in the same season.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domestic_broadcasters">Domestic broadcasters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Domestic broadcasters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/English_football_on_television" title="English football on television">English football on television</a></div>
<p>The FA Cup Final is one of 10 events reserved for live broadcast on UK terrestrial television under the <a href="/wiki/Ofcom_Code_on_Sports_and_Other_Listed_and_Designated_Events" title="Ofcom Code on Sports and Other Listed and Designated Events">Ofcom Code on Sports and Other Listed and Designated Events</a>.
</p><p>In the early years of coverage the BBC had exclusive radio coverage with a picture of the pitch marked in the <a href="/wiki/Radio_Times" title="Radio Times">Radio Times</a> with numbered squares to help the listener follow the match on the radio. The first FA Cup Final on Radio was in 1926 between Bolton Wanderers and Manchester City but this was only broadcast in Manchester, the first national final on BBC Radio was between Arsenal and Cardiff in 1927. The first final on BBC Television was in 1937 in a match which featured Sunderland and Preston North End but this was not televised in full. The following season's final between Preston and Huddersfield was covered in full by the BBC. When ITV was formed in 1955 they shared final coverage with the BBC in one of the only club matches shown live on television, during the 1970s and 1980s coverage became more elaborate with BBC and ITV trying to steal viewers from the others by starting coverage earlier and earlier some starting as early as 9&#160;a.m. which was six hours before kick off. The sharing of rights between BBC and ITV continued from 1955 to 1988, when ITV lost coverage to the new Sports Channel which later became <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a>.
</p><p>From 1988 to 1997, the BBC and Sky Sports had coverage of the FA Cup, the BBC had highlights on Match of the Day and usually one match per round while Sky had the same deal. From 1997 to 2001, ITV and Sky shared live coverage with both having two matches per round and BBC continuing with highlights on Match of the Day. From 2002 to 2008, BBC and Sky again shared coverage with BBC having two or three matches per round and Sky having one or two. From <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_FA_Cup" title="2008–09 FA Cup">2008–09</a> to <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_FA_Cup" title="2013–14 FA Cup">2013–14</a>, FA Cup matches are shown live by <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_channel)" title="ITV (TV channel)">ITV</a> across England and <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>, with <a href="/wiki/UTV_(TV_channel)" title="UTV (TV channel)">UTV</a> broadcasting to <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">Northern Ireland</a> but STV refusing to show them. ITV shows 16 FA Cup games per season, including the first pick of live matches from each of the first to sixth rounds of the competition, plus one semi-final exclusively live. The final is also shown live on ITV. Under the same 2008 contract, <a href="/wiki/Setanta_Sports" title="Setanta Sports">Setanta Sports</a> showed three games and one replay in each round from round three to five, two quarter-finals, one semi-final and the final. The channel also broadcast ITV's matches exclusively to <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, after the ITV franchise holder in Scotland, <a href="/wiki/STV_(TV_network)" class="mw-redirect" title="STV (TV network)">STV</a>, decided not to broadcast FA Cup games. Setanta entered administration in June 2009 and as a result the FA terminated Setanta's deal to broadcast FA-sanctioned competitions and <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England internationals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> As a result of Setanta going out of business ITV showed the competition exclusively in the 2009–10 season with between three and four matches per round, all quarter finals, semi-finals and final live as the FA could not find a pay TV broadcaster in time. ESPN bought the competition for the 2010–11 to 2012–13 season and during this time Rebecca Lowe became the first woman to host the FA Cup Final in the UK.
</p><p>In October 2009, The FA announced that ITV would show an additional match in the First and Second Rounds on ITV, with one replay match shown on <a href="/wiki/ITV4" title="ITV4">ITV4</a>. One match and one replay match from the first two rounds will broadcast on The FA website for free, in a similar situation to the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2010 World Cup Qualifier</a> between <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_national_football_team" title="Ukraine national football team">Ukraine</a> and <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The 2009–10 First Round match between <a href="/wiki/Oldham_Athletic_A.F.C." title="Oldham Athletic A.F.C.">Oldham Athletic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_A.F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds United A.F.C.">Leeds United</a> was the first FA Cup match to be streamed online live.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2011)">who?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> expected <a href="/wiki/BSkyB" class="mw-redirect" title="BSkyB">BSkyB</a> to make a bid to show some of the remaining FA Cup games for the remainder of the 2009–10 season which would include a semi-final and shared rights to the final. <a href="/wiki/ESPN_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="ESPN (UK)">ESPN</a> took over the package Setanta held for the FA Cup from the 2010–11 season.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The 2011 final was also shown live on <a href="/wiki/Sky_3D" title="Sky 3D">Sky 3D</a> in addition to ESPN (who provided the 3D coverage for Sky 3D) and ITV.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Following the sale of ESPN's UK and Ireland channels to <a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT</a>, ESPN's rights package transferred to <a href="/wiki/BT_Sport" title="BT Sport">BT Sport</a> from the 2013–14 season.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">BBC Radio 5 Live</a> and <a href="/wiki/Talksport" title="Talksport">Talksport</a> provides radio coverage including several full live commentaries per round, with additional commentaries broadcast on <a href="/wiki/BBC_Local_Radio" title="BBC Local Radio">BBC Local Radio</a>.
</p><p>Until the 2008–09 season, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> shared television coverage, with the BBC showing three matches in the earlier rounds. Some analysts argued the decision to move away from the Sky and, in particular, the BBC undermined the FA Cup in the eyes of the public.
</p><p>The early rounds of the 2008–09 competition were covered for the first time by ITV's online service, <a href="/wiki/ITV_Local" title="ITV Local">ITV Local</a>. The first match of the competition, between Wantage Town and Brading Town, was broadcast live online. Highlights of eight games of each round were broadcast as catch up on ITV Local.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Since ITV Local closed, this coverage did not continue.
</p><p>ITV lost the rights to the FA Cup beginning with the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_FA_Cup" title="2014–15 FA Cup">2014–15 FA Cup</a>, terrestrial rights will return to <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a>, with the final being shown on <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> while BT Sport hold the pay TV rights. Under this deal, the BBC will show around the same number of games as ITV and still having the first pick for each round.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Matches involving Welsh clubs are sometimes exclusively broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh language</a> channel <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">S4C</a>, which is also available to view across the rest of the United Kingdom on satellite and cable television, and through the channel's website.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> A similar arrangement is shared with <a href="/wiki/BBC_Cymru_Wales" title="BBC Cymru Wales">BBC Cymru Wales</a> from 2014–15, potentially giving the BBC an extra match per round.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overseas_broadcasters">Overseas broadcasters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Overseas broadcasters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_FA_Cup_broadcasters" title="List of FA Cup broadcasters">List of FA Cup broadcasters</a></div>
<p>The FA sells overseas rights separately from the domestic contract. 
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-29598744">"Oldest football cup 'not for sale<span class="cs1-kern-right">'</span>"</a>. <i>BBC News</i>. 14 October 2014. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20171105114055/http://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-29598744">Archived</a> from the original on 5 November 2017<span class="reference-accessdate">. <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=FA_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since 1920, when the Football League expanded to three divisions, no club from outside the top two divisions has reached the final. Since 1914, when QPR reached the fourth round proper (the last eight/quarter-final stage), the only non-league club to have reached that stage is Lincoln City in 2017.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
